https://i1.wp.com/bloody-disgusting.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/09/Family-Portraits-Trilogy-of-America-Cutting-Moments.jpg?resize=1024%2C512&#38;ssl=1 1024w, https://i1.wp.com/bloody-disgusting.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/09/Family-Portraits-Trilogy-of-America-Cutting-Moments.jpg?resize=768%2C384&#38;ssl=1 768w\" sizes=\"(max-width: 740px) 100vw, 740px\" data-recalc-dims=\"1\" /></a></p>\n<p><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\">Filmed around the mid-nineties, the segments in this sometimes graphic drama vary from lethargic to utterly shocking. Director Douglas Buck does not bother with formalities as he delves straight into the incredibly grotesque and disturbing &#8220;Cutting Moments.&#8221; A housewife is torn between her maternal obligations and her own desires within a failing marriage. Her husband&#8217;s mind is elsewhere and the matriarch will do whatever it takes to finally seize his attention. Here, the appetizer winds up being better than the actual meal.</span></p>\n<hr />\n<h2><b><i>The Willies: </i></b><b>(1990) — &#8220;Bad Apples&#8221;</b></h2>\n<p><a href=\"https://i2.wp.com/bloody-disgusting.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/09/Willies.jpg?ssl=1\"><img data-attachment-id=\"3630580\" data-image-meta=\"{&#34;aperture&#34;:&#34;0&#34;,&#34;credit&#34;:&#34;&#34;,&#34;camera&#34;:&#34;&#34;,&#34;caption&#34;:&#34;&#34;,&#34;created_timestamp&#34;:&#34;0&#34;,&#34;copyright&#34;:&#34;&#34;,&#34;focal_length&#34;:&#34;0&#34;,&#34;iso&#34;:&#34;0&#34;,&#34;shutter_speed&#34;:&#34;0&#34;,&#34;title&#34;:&#34;&#34;,&#34;orientation&#34;:&#34;0&#34;}\" data-image-title=\"Willies\" data-image-description=\"\" data-medium-file=\"https://i2.wp.com/bloody-disgusting.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/09/Willies.jpg?fit=300%2C229&#38;ssl=1\" srcset=\"https://i2.wp.com/bloody-disgusting.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/09/Willies.jpg?w=1200&#38;ssl=1 1200w, https://i2.wp.com/bloody-disgusting.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/09/Willies.jpg?resize=300%2C229&#38;ssl=1 300w, https://i2.wp.com/bloody-disgusting.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/09/Willies.jpg?resize=1024%2C782&#38;ssl=1 1024w, https://i2.wp.com/bloody-disgusting.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/09/Willies.jpg?resize=768%2C586&#38;ssl=1 768w\" sizes=\"(max-width: 740px) 100vw, 740px\" data-recalc-dims=\"1\" /></a></p>\n<p><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\">This juvenile anthology often looks and acts like a spiritual extension of </span><i><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\">Are You Afraid of the Dark?</span></i><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\"> albeit more bloody and scuzzy. The narrative format is unconventional, but the longer segments are agreeable. &#8220;Bad Apples&#8221; is a wonderful update of &#8220;The Boy Who Cried Wolf&#8221; except the wolf is a monster who lives in the school restroom. The more Danny swears the creature exists, the more his acerbic teacher refuses to believe him. That is, until it&#8217;s too late to change her mind.</span></p>\n<hr />\n<h2><b><i>Chillers: </i></b><b>(1987) — Mason&#8217;s Story</b></h2>\n<p><a href=\"https://i1.wp.com/bloody-disgusting.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/09/Chillers.jpg?ssl=1\"><img data-attachment-id=\"3630581\" data-permalink=\"https://bloody-disgusting.com/editorials/3630549/30-standout-segments-underseen-horror-anthology-movies/attachment/chillers-2/\" data-orig-file=\"https://i1.wp.com/bloody-disgusting.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/09/Chillers.jpg?fit=1200%2C916&#38;ssl=1\" data-orig-size=\"1200,916\" data-comments-opened=\"1\" data-image-meta=\"{&#34;aperture&#34;:&#34;0&#34;,&#34;credit&#34;:&#34;&#34;,&#34;camera&#34;:&#34;&#34;,&#34;caption&#34;:&#34;&#34;,&#34;created_timestamp&#34;:&#34;0&#34;,&#34;copyright&#34;:&#34;&#34;,&#34;focal_length&#34;:&#34;0&#34;,&#34;iso&#34;:&#34;0&#34;,&#34;shutter_speed&#34;:&#34;0&#34;,&#34;title&#34;:&#34;&#34;,&#34;orientation&#34;:&#34;0&#34;}\" data-image-title=\"Chillers\" data-image-description=\"\" data-medium-file=\"https://i1.wp.com/bloody-disgusting.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/09/Chillers.jpg?fit=300%2C229&#38;ssl=1\" data-large-file=\"https://i1.wp.com/bloody-disgusting.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/09/Chillers.jpg?fit=740%2C565&#38;ssl=1\" class=\"alignnone size-full wp-image-3630581\" src=\"https://i1.wp.com/bloody-disgusting.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/09/Chillers.jpg?resize=740%2C565&#038;ssl=1\" alt=\"\" width=\"740\" height=\"565\" srcset=\"https://i1.wp.com/bloody-disgusting.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/09/Chillers.jpg?w=1200&#38;ssl=1 1200w, https://i1.wp.com/bloody-disgusting.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/09/Chillers.jpg?resize=300%2C229&#38;ssl=1 300w, https://i1.wp.com/bloody-disgusting.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/09/Chillers.jpg?resize=1024%2C782&#38;ssl=1 1024w, https://i1.wp.com/bloody-disgusting.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/09/Chillers.jpg?resize=768%2C586&#38;ssl=1 768w\" sizes=\"(max-width: 740px) 100vw, 740px\" data-recalc-dims=\"1\" /></a></p>\n<p><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\">Daniel Boyd&#8217;s debut feature </span><i><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\">Chillers</span></i><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\"> is as earnest as it is cheesy. The actual content isn&#8217;t all that exciting, but there is the occasional bright spot in this West Virginia-shot anthology. In the same vein as 1973&#8217;s </span><i><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\">The Vault of Horror</span></i><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\">, the main characters pass the time at a bus station by sharing their portentous dreams. Young Mason, who is on his way to a scout camp, describes his recent nightmare — he and several other boys are menaced by a bloodthirsty madman while out in the woods. This story utilizes its environment the best, and there is some genuine tension.</span></p>\n<hr />\n<h2><b><i>Deadtime Stories: </i></b><b>(1986) — &#8220;Little Red Runninghood&#8221;</b></h2>\n<p><a href=\"https://i1.wp.com/bloody-disgusting.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/09/Deadtime-Stories-1986.jpg?ssl=1\"><img data-attachment-id=\"3630582\" data-permalink=\"https://bloody-disgusting.com/editorials/3630549/30-standout-segments-underseen-horror-anthology-movies/attachment/deadtime-stories-1986/\" data-orig-file=\"https://i1.wp.com/bloody-disgusting.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/09/Deadtime-Stories-1986.jpg?fit=1200%2C600&#38;ssl=1\" data-orig-size=\"1200,600\" data-comments-opened=\"1\" data-image-meta=\"{&#34;aperture&#34;:&#34;0&#34;,&#34;credit&#34;:&#34;&#34;,&#34;camera&#34;:&#34;&#34;,&#34;caption&#34;:&#34;&#34;,&#34;created_timestamp&#34;:&#34;0&#34;,&#34;copyright&#34;:&#34;&#34;,&#34;focal_length&#34;:&#34;0&#34;,&#34;iso&#34;:&#34;0&#34;,&#34;shutter_speed&#34;:&#34;0&#34;,&#34;title&#34;:&#34;&#34;,&#34;orientation&#34;:&#34;0&#34;}\" data-image-title=\"Deadtime-Stories-1986\" data-image-description=\"\" data-medium-file=\"https://i1.wp.com/bloody-disgusting.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/09/Deadtime-Stories-1986.jpg?fit=300%2C150&#38;ssl=1\" data-large-file=\"https://i1.wp.com/bloody-disgusting.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/09/Deadtime-Stories-1986.jpg?fit=740%2C370&#38;ssl=1\" class=\"alignnone size-full wp-image-3630582\" src=\"https://i1.wp.com/bloody-disgusting.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/09/Deadtime-Stories-1986.jpg?resize=740%2C370&#038;ssl=1\" alt=\"\" width=\"740\" height=\"370\" srcset=\"https://i1.wp.com/bloody-disgusting.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/09/Deadtime-Stories-1986.jpg?w=1200&#38;ssl=1 1200w, https://i1.wp.com/bloody-disgusting.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/09/Deadtime-Stories-1986.jpg?resize=300%2C150&#38;ssl=1 300w, https://i1.wp.com/bloody-disgusting.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/09/Deadtime-Stories-1986.jpg?resize=1024%2C512&#38;ssl=1 1024w, https://i1.wp.com/bloody-disgusting.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/09/Deadtime-Stories-1986.jpg?resize=768%2C384&#38;ssl=1 768w\" sizes=\"(max-width: 740px) 100vw, 740px\" data-recalc-dims=\"1\" /></a></p>\n<p><i><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\">Deadtime Stories</span></i><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\">&#8216; wraparound has an impatient uncle telling his scared nephew morbid fairy tales before bedtime. To no one&#8217;s surprise but his own, Uncle Mike&#8217;s counterintuitive decision only exacerbates the boy&#8217;s fear, and he spends the night entertaining Peter with more horrid fables. One of which is an amusing spoof of &#8220;Little Red Riding Hood;&#8221; a teen decked in red ends up with the wrong bag when picking up her grandmother&#8217;s medication at the pharmacy. Unfortunately, the prescription she takes home is for a werewolf, and he&#8217;s decided to pay Granny a visit.</span></p>\n<hr />\n<h2><b><i>The Illustrated Man: </i></b><b>(1969) — &#8220;The Veldt&#8221;</b></h2>\n<p><a href=\"https://i1.wp.com/bloody-disgusting.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/09/Illustrated-Man.jpg?ssl=1\"><img data-attachment-id=\"3630583\" data-permalink=\"https://bloody-disgusting.com/editorials/3630549/30-standout-segments-underseen-horror-anthology-movies/attachment/illustrated-man/\" data-orig-file=\"https://i1.wp.com/bloody-disgusting.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/09/Illustrated-Man.jpg?fit=1200%2C600&#38;ssl=1\" data-orig-size=\"1200,600\" data-comments-opened=\"1\" data-image-meta=\"{&#34;aperture&#34;:&#34;0&#34;,&#34;credit&#34;:&#34;&#34;,&#34;camera&#34;:&#34;&#34;,&#34;caption&#34;:&#34;&#34;,&#34;created_timestamp&#34;:&#34;0&#34;,&#34;copyright&#34;:&#34;&#34;,&#34;focal_length&#34;:&#34;0&#34;,&#34;iso&#34;:&#34;0&#34;,&#34;shutter_speed&#34;:&#34;0&#34;,&#34;title&#34;:&#34;&#34;,&#34;orientation&#34;:&#34;0&#34;}\" data-image-title=\"Illustrated-Man\" data-image-description=\"\" data-medium-file=\"https://i1.wp.com/bloody-disgusting.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/09/Illustrated-Man.jpg?fit=300%2C150&#38;ssl=1\" data-large-file=\"https://i1.wp.com/bloody-disgusting.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/09/Illustrated-Man.jpg?fit=740%2C370&#38;ssl=1\" class=\"alignnone size-full wp-image-3630583\" src=\"https://i1.wp.com/bloody-disgusting.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/09/Illustrated-Man.jpg?resize=740%2C370&#038;ssl=1\" alt=\"\" width=\"740\" height=\"370\" srcset=\"https://i1.wp.com/bloody-disgusting.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/09/Illustrated-Man.jpg?w=1200&#38;ssl=1 1200w, https://i1.wp.com/bloody-disgusting.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/09/Illustrated-Man.jpg?resize=300%2C150&#38;ssl=1 300w, https://i1.wp.com/bloody-disgusting.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/09/Illustrated-Man.jpg?resize=1024%2C512&#38;ssl=1 1024w, https://i1.wp.com/bloody-disgusting.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/09/Illustrated-Man.jpg?resize=768%2C384&#38;ssl=1 768w\" sizes=\"(max-width: 740px) 100vw, 740px\" data-recalc-dims=\"1\" /></a></p>\n<p><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\">Ray Bradbury&#8217;s book of the same name is the basis for this divisive adaptation. The movie wound up being a critical and financial flop, and the author himself was not a fan. Be that as it may, the film has artistic merit in addition to intense performances. </span><i><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\">The Illustrated Man</span></i><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\"> plays out like </span><i><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\">The Canterbury Tales</span></i><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\">; the stories within accentuate rather than detract from the main one. The suggestive chemistry between Rod Steiger and Robert Drivas&#8217; characters is another draw.</span></p>\n<p><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\">Between &#8220;The Veldt&#8221; and &#8220;The Long Rain,&#8221; the former feels the most complete. A family of the future is in trouble because the children are consumed with their virtual reality nursery. When the parents threaten to take it away, their progeny retaliate. There is no denying the white interiors, décor, and general aesthetic were inspired by that of </span><i><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\">2001: A Space Odyssey</span></i><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\">.</span></p>\n<hr />\n<h2><b><i>The Curse of Kazuo Umezu: </i></b><b>(1990) — &#8220;The Haunted Mansion&#8221;</b></h2>\n<p><a href=\"https://i0.wp.com/bloody-disgusting.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/09/Curse-of-Kazuo-Umezu.jpg?ssl=1\"><img data-attachment-id=\"3630584\" data-permalink=\"https://bloody-disgusting.com/editorials/3630549/30-standout-segments-underseen-horror-anthology-movies/attachment/curse-of-kazuo-umezu/\" data-orig-file=\"https://i0.wp.com/bloody-disgusting.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/09/Curse-of-Kazuo-Umezu.jpg?fit=1200%2C916&#38;ssl=1\" data-orig-size=\"1200,916\" data-comments-opened=\"1\" data-image-meta=\"{&#34;aperture&#34;:&#34;0&#34;,&#34;credit&#34;:&#34;&#34;,&#34;camera&#34;:&#34;&#34;,&#34;caption&#34;:&#34;&#34;,&#34;created_timestamp&#34;:&#34;0&#34;,&#34;copyright&#34;:&#34;&#34;,&#34;focal_length&#34;:&#34;0&#34;,&#34;iso&#34;:&#34;0&#34;,&#34;shutter_speed&#34;:&#34;0&#34;,&#34;title&#34;:&#34;&#34;,&#34;orientation&#34;:&#34;0&#34;}\" data-image-title=\"Curse-of-Kazuo-Umezu\" data-image-description=\"\" data-medium-file=\"https://i0.wp.com/bloody-disgusting.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/09/Curse-of-Kazuo-Umezu.jpg?fit=300%2C229&#38;ssl=1\" data-large-file=\"https://i0.wp.com/bloody-disgusting.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/09/Curse-of-Kazuo-Umezu.jpg?fit=740%2C565&#38;ssl=1\" class=\"alignnone size-full wp-image-3630584\" src=\"https://i0.wp.com/bloody-disgusting.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/09/Curse-of-Kazuo-Umezu.jpg?resize=740%2C565&#038;ssl=1\" alt=\"\" width=\"740\" height=\"565\" srcset=\"https://i0.wp.com/bloody-disgusting.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/09/Curse-of-Kazuo-Umezu.jpg?w=1200&#38;ssl=1 1200w, https://i0.wp.com/bloody-disgusting.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/09/Curse-of-Kazuo-Umezu.jpg?resize=300%2C229&#38;ssl=1 300w, https://i0.wp.com/bloody-disgusting.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/09/Curse-of-Kazuo-Umezu.jpg?resize=1024%2C782&#38;ssl=1 1024w, https://i0.wp.com/bloody-disgusting.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/09/Curse-of-Kazuo-Umezu.jpg?resize=768%2C586&#38;ssl=1 768w\" sizes=\"(max-width: 740px) 100vw, 740px\" data-recalc-dims=\"1\" /></a></p>\n<p><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\">One of Junji Itō&#8217;s biggest influences is esteemed manga author Kazuo Umezu. Known for his detailed and macabre illustrations, Umezu is also adept at emphasizing raw human emotions in the presence of horror.  His ability to capture freeze frames of intense inwardness — those deep, heightened feelings that surface upon seeing something so unspeakable — is nothing short of brilliant.</span></p>\n<p><i><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\">The Curse of Kazuo Umezu</span></i><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\"> is a straight-to-video anthology featuring two standalone stories. Although each one is positively crude-looking by today&#8217;s standards, the artwork has a lot of character to it. &#8220;What Will the Video Camera Reveal&#8221; includes a vampiric, tentacle-faced demon, and &#8220;The Haunted Mansion&#8221; has four girls exploring a sinister old house. Neither short will disappoint fans of anime horror, but the timeless appeal of the second tale is hard to resist.</span></p>\n<img 16:45:25","updatedTime":"2020-09-05 16:45:25","title":"Bethesda Enlists Andrew Hulshult For Upcoming ‘DOOM Eternal’ DLC","link":"https://bloody-disgusting.com/?p=3630503","description":"<p>After the <a href=\"https://bloody-disgusting.com/video-games/3615272/id-software-responds-doom-eternal-composer-mick-gordons-claims/\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener noreferrer\">less-than-amicable split</a> between <strong><em>DOOM Eternal</em></strong> composer Mick Gordon and Bethesda, it was a question of who would replace Gordon in the upcoming &#8220;The Ancient Gods&#8221; DLC expansion. Well, who better to conduct a sonic assault in a shooter than someone who&#8217;s been doing that for more than a while?</p>\n<p>That&#8217;s right, <strong>Andrew Hulshult</strong>, who has scored throwback shooters like <strong><em>DUSK</em></strong>, the <strong><em>Brutal Doom</em></strong> mod (which is <a href=\"https://www.moddb.com/mods/brutal-doom/addons/idkfa-doom-soundtrack\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener noreferrer\">available for free</a>, so get it), <strong><em>Wrath: Aeon of Ruin</em></strong> and the upcoming <strong><em>Prodeus</em></strong>, is doing what&#8217;s necessary to ensure ripping and tearing in <em>DOOM Eternal</em> remains as such.</p>\n<p>Hulshult made the announcement on Twitter that he will be collaborating with id Software engineer David Levy, who had stepped in to finish up the <em>DOOM Eternal</em> soundtrack after difficulties with Gordon became apparent.</p>\n<p><em>The Ancient Gods, Part One</em>, will launch on October 20th for PC, PlayStation 4 and Xbox One. PlayStation 5, Xbox Series X, and Switch versions of <em>DOOM Eternal</em> are also planned for release.</p>\n<blockquote class=\"twitter-tweet\">\n<p dir=\"ltr\" lang=\"en\">Unbelievably happy to href=\"https://twitter.com/DavidLevyMusic?ref_src=twsrc%5Etfw\">@DavidLevyMusic</a> !<br />\nBuckle up! <img src=\"https://s.w.org/images/core/emoji/12.0.0-1/72x72/1f642.png\" alt=\"🙂\" Records","link":"https://bloody-disgusting.com/?p=3630391","description":"<p>For the first time ever, the original motion picture soundtracks for <strong>Rob Zombie</strong>&#8216;s<strong><em> Halloween</em></strong> and<strong><em> Halloween II</em> </strong>release on vinyl this Halloween season, via <strong>Waxwork Records</strong>!</p>\n<p>For <em>Halloween</em>, the deluxe double LP features score cues by composer Tyler Bates, select dialogue from the movie, and soundtrack songs including tracks by Alice Cooper, The Misfits, Blue Öyster Cult, Nazareth, Peter Frampton, Kiss, Iggy Pop, and more. The packaging features 180 gram Black and Crystal Clear Striped Vinyl with Pumpkin Orange Splatter, exclusive liner notes by Rob Zombie, a 12”x12” twenty page booklet featuring never-before-seen set photography from Zombie’s personal collection, a 12”x12” art print insert, printed inner LP sleeves featuring set photography, old style tip-on gatefold jackets with matte satin coating, and new artwork by Robert Sammelin.</p>\n<p>And for <em>Halloween II</em>, the deluxe release features score cues by Tyler Bates, select dialogue from the movie, and soundtrack songs including tracks by The Moody Blues, Motörhead, Void, Scream, Foghat, Captain Clegg and the Nightcreatures, and more. The packaging features 180 gram Pumpkin Orange, Candy Apple Red, and Magenta swirled colored vinyl, exclusive liner notes by Rob Zombie, a 12”x12” twenty Page booklet featuring never-before-seen set photography from Zombie’s personal collection, a 12”x12” art print insert, printed inner LP sleeves featuring set photography, old style tip-on gatefold jackets with matte satin coating, and new artwork by Robert Sammelin.</p>\n<p><a href=\"https://waxworkrecords.com/collections/vinyl\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener noreferrer\">Both soundtracks are up for pre-order right now, shipping on 16:45:25","updatedTime":"2020-09-05 16:45:25","title":"‘Vampire’s Fall: Origins’ Arrives on Xbox One And Switch September 17th","link":"https://bloody-disgusting.com/?p=3630151","description":"<p><a href=\"https://bloody-disgusting.com/video-games/3623660/dark-throwback-rpg-vampires-fall-origins-announced-xbox-one-nintendo-switch/\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener noreferrer\">Back in July</a>, Early Morning Studio had announced that their throwback RPG <strong><em>Vampire’s Fall: Origins</em></strong> would be headed to the Xbox One and Nintendo Switch this Fall. Well, that time is right around the corner, as the devs announced that the game will launch on those consoles on September 17th.</p>\n<p>“<em>Vampire’s Fall</em> has come a long way since the first time we came up with the concept,” said Emir Kuljanin from Early Morning Studio. “Now 10 years later and three platforms in, we are gearing up for Nintendo Switch and Xbox One launch to welcome console players into the gritty and witty world full of mystery.”</p>\n<p>After the malevolent Witchmaster destroys the Vamp’Ire village, you awaken as a fledgling vampire set on a course for revenge. Your efforts to halt the dark magic conjurings of your evil foe take you on a journey through a vast 2D open world where you embark on quests, encounter a variety of NPCs, and face scores of enemies through over 50 hours of gameplay, leveling up your character by unlocking skills and abilities as well as upgrading your gear along the way.</p>\n<p>You can also grab the game <a href=\"https://store.steampowered.com/app/1167950/Vampires_Fall_Origins/\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener noreferrer\">on Steam</a>.</p>\n<img src=\"http://feeds.feedburner.com/~r/BloodyDisgusting/~4/NMTFuY3fWQ4\" height=\"1\" width=\"1\" alt=\"\"/>","descriptionType":"html","publishedDate":"Wed, 02 Sep 2020 23:43:05 +0000","feedId":13077,"bgimg":"","linkMd5":"348e621900e5ab96b5b34009889758d7","bgimgJsdelivr":"","metaImg":"","author":"Mike Wilson","articleImgCdnMap":{"http://feeds.feedburner.com/~r/BloodyDisgusting/~4/NMTFuY3fWQ4":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx5oss/cdn21@2020_5/2020/09/05/08-45-57-806_0e9ae7bdb56b0f20.webp"},"publishedOrCreatedDate":1599295525722},{"createdTime":"2020-09-05 16:45:25","updatedTime":"2020-09-05 16:45:25","title":"[R.I.P.] ‘Killer Klowns from Outer Space’ Actor Peter Licassi Has Passed Away","link":"https://bloody-disgusting.com/?p=3630272","description":"<p>We&#8217;ve learned the sad news via <strong><em>Killer Klowns from Outer Space</em></strong> co-star/friend Michael Siegel that <strong>Peter Licassi</strong>, who played the lovable ice cream man Paul Terenzi in 1988&#8217;s horror-comedy, passed away on August 27th. Tragically, Licassi took his own life at 61.</p>\n<p><a href=\"https://www.facebook.com/michael.siegel.7/posts/10220859570651657\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener noreferrer\">Siegel writes over on Facebook</a>, &#8220;On Thursday August 27th 2020, my friend, my brother, my partner in comedy Peter Licassi lost his battle with depression and took his own life. Peter had been struggling with depression for many years choosing to live a very private life. In the prime of his life, Peter was incredibly talented. Funny, clever, an accomplished musician (man, could he play the banjo), a wonderful actor and a brilliant comedian. His timing was impeccable and his ability to take an idea and turn it into an entertaining routine was his gift.&#8221;</p>\n<p>&#8220;But Peter was more than that. He was kind and generous and supportive and would do anything for you,&#8221; Siegel continues. &#8220;He was tough too. He always stood up for what he believed in. He was a perfectionist and at times those moments were difficult to handle. But he was honest, protective and caring. I was fortunate to have worked side by side on stage (me on his left, he on my right in perfect harmony) with him for 16 years and even more fortunate to have been his friend for 38 years and learn what a true friendship can be. I will never forget the laughs we shared, the success we had and the tears we cried together. From now and for the rest of my life whenever I look to my right I will see my friend, my brother, my partner enjoying the hell out of life.&#8221;</p>\n<p>Siegel adds, &#8220;<strong>If you or someone you know is suffering from depression please, please, please don&#8217;t be afraid or embarrassed to talk to someone. If you live in the UK please call the suicide prevention hotline 116 123. If you live in the States please call 1-800 448 1833</strong>.&#8221;</p>\n<p><em>Killer Klowns</em> creators the <a href=\"https://www.facebook.com/ChiodoBros/posts/3737983286229273\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener noreferrer\">Chiodo Brothers also paid tribute to Licassi on their Facebook page</a>, writing: &#8220;It&#8217;s with great sadness that we share this terrible news. Pete will forever be in our hearts and his memory will live on. Our condolences to his family and brother in life, Michael Siegel. Depression is real and a serious illness. If you suffer from depression, don&#8217;t be afraid to reach out and ask for help. Rest in peace our dear friend, Peter Licassi aka Paul Terenzi.&#8221;</p>\n<p>If you are suffering from depression, the National Suicide Prevention Lifeline can be dialed 24/7 at 1-800-273-8255. The Lifeline provides free and confidential support for people in distress, prevention and crisis resources, and best practices for professionals.</p>\n<p><iframe class='youtube-player' width='740' height='417' src='https://www.youtube.com/embed/PC4wbTAa5SI?version=3&#038;rel=1&#038;fs=1&#038;autohide=2&#038;showsearch=0&#038;showinfo=1&#038;iv_load_policy=1&#038;start=35&#038;wmode=transparent' allowfullscreen='true' style='border:0;'></iframe></p>\n<img src=\"http://feeds.feedburner.com/~r/BloodyDisgusting/~4/NddpCTjGEVA\" height=\"1\" width=\"1\" alt=\"\"/>","descriptionType":"html","publishedDate":"Wed, 02 Sep 2020 18:55:40 +0000","feedId":13077,"bgimg":"","linkMd5":"9f5a6aa91474ea88d93cf64899f3ff95","bgimgJsdelivr":"","metaImg":"","author":"John Squires","articleImgCdnMap":{"http://feeds.feedburner.com/~r/BloodyDisgusting/~4/NddpCTjGEVA":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx22/cdn25@2020_5/2020/09/05/08-45-58-638_6ce22b5f87b86852.webp"},"publishedOrCreatedDate":1599295525723},{"createdTime":"2020-09-05 16:45:25","updatedTime":"2020-09-05 16:45:25","title":"Psychological Horror ‘A Banquet’ Tests the Faith of HanWay Films","link":"https://bloody-disgusting.com/?p=3630353","description":"<p>HanWay Films has boarded worldwide sales on <strong>Ruth Paxton</strong>’s directorial debut, the psychological horror <em><strong>A Banquet</strong></em>, Bloody Disgusting learned Thursday morning.</p>\n<p>Sounding like a mix between <em>Exorcist</em> and the forthcoming <em>Saint Maud</em>, &#8220;Widowed mother Holly is radically tested when her teenage daughter Betsey (<strong>Jessica Alexander</strong>) experiences profound enlightenment and insists that her body is no longer her own, but in service to a higher power. Bound to her newfound faith Betsey refuses to eat, but loses no weight. In an agonizing dilemma torn between love and fear, Holly is forced to confront the boundaries of her own beliefs.&#8221;</p>\n<p><em>A Banquet</em> also stars <strong>Sienna Guillory</strong> (<em>Resident Evil</em> series, <em>High Rise</em>), <strong>Ruby Stokes</strong> (<em>Rocks, Una</em>), and award-winning actress <strong>Lindsay Duncan CBE</strong> (<em>Made in Italy, Private Lives</em>).</p>\n<p>The feature is written by AFI alumnus <strong>Justin Bull</strong> and was shot on location in London during July and August 2020.</p>\n<p>Producers on the picture are Leonora Darby, Mark Lane and James Harris for Tea Shop Productions (<em>47 Meters Down, I Am Not A Serial Killer, Cockneys Vs Zombies</em>), Nik Bower (<em>Final Portrait, The Wedding Guest</em>) for Riverstone Pictures and Laure Vaysse (<em>Tell It to the Bees</em>) for REP Productions 8 Ltd, which also funded the production.</p>\n<p>Deepak Nayar of Motion Picture Capital serves as Executive Producer, alongside Jeremy Baxter of Riverstone Pictures and Patrick Fischer and Richard Kondal of Creativity Capital.</p>\n<img src=\"http://feeds.feedburner.com/~r/BloodyDisgusting/~4/mbIl8hP6gus\" <strong>&#8220;Welcome to the Blumhouse&#8221;</strong>, a program of <em>eight</em> unsettling genre movies with each film presenting a distinctive vision and unique perspective on common themes centered around family and love as redemptive or destructive forces.</span></p>\n<p>The first <strong><em>four</em></strong> Blumhouse-produced movies are all arriving for <em>free</em> on Amazon Prime this fall as double features starting on <strong>October 6</strong> with <strong><i>The Lie</i></strong> directed by acclaimed writer/director <strong>Veena Sud</strong> (<i>The Killing, 7 Seconds</i>) and <i><strong>Black Box</strong> </i>directed by up-and-coming writer/director <strong>Emmanuel Osei-Kuffour Jr.</strong> (<i>Born with It</i>).</p>\n<p>Launching the following week on <strong>October 13</strong> is <strong><i>Evil Eye</i></strong>, from talented young directors <strong>Elan Dassani </strong>and<strong> Rajeev Dassani</strong> (<i>A Day’s Work, Jinn</i>) and executive produced by Priyanka Chopra Jonas (<i>Quantico, White Tiger</i>), and <strong><i>Nocturne</i></strong> written and directed by filmmaker <strong>Zu Quirke</strong> (<i>Zugzwang</i>, <i>Ghosting</i>) making her feature film debut.</p>\n<p>The teaser trailer is here and asks viewers to &#8220;unsettle in&#8221; didn&#8217;t take long. <a href=\"https://bloody-disgusting.com/video-games/3627952/lovecraftian-digital-board-game-october-night-games-turns-kickstarter-will-arrive-steam-october-15/\" rel=\"noopener noreferrer\" target=\"_blank\">Announced two weeks ago</a>, October Night Games&#8217; digital board game of the same name has met its Kickstarter funding goal of €5,000. Every little bit helps, as they say, and there are still <a href=\"https://www.kickstarter.com/projects/octobernightgames/october-night-games/posts\" rel=\"noopener noreferrer\" target=\"_blank\">plenty of stretch goals to hit.</a></p>\n<p>On top of that, the devs have revealed a new demo that <a href=\"https://store.steampowered.com/app/1334580/October_Night_Games/\" rel=\"noopener noreferrer\" target=\"_blank\">you can download today</a>. The demo will offers up a unique mode in the Dream Quest: </p>\n<p>You summon Nyarlathotep to pass a trial for the Great Game. As a result, the Crawling Chaos plunges you into a dream indistinguishable from reality, where you find yourself in a small town with five other players. As in the base game, you search for ingredients and perform rituals. However, in Dream Quest mode, you only have 15 nights until the moon dies. During this time, you need to figure out who is in your team and who is in the enemy team. Only by choosing the right allies, you can prove yourself worthy to participate in the Halloween full moon ritual and wake up.</p>\n<p>Unlike the base game, you&#8217;ll only have access to three characters (The Werewolf, The Mad Monk, and Madame Mandilip with her dolls) and three familiars (the guide dog, the pathfinder cat, and the wise owl). The devs are planning updates for the demo, so stay tuned for that.</p>\n<p><em>October Night Games</em> is scheduled for an October 15th release on Steam.</p>\n<img src=\"http://feeds.feedburner.com/~r/BloodyDisgusting/~4/jCj4iTSlFbE\" height=\"1\" width=\"1\" alt=\"\"/>","descriptionType":"html","publishedDate":"Thu, 03 Sep 2020 13:32:04 +0000","feedId":13077,"bgimg":"","linkMd5":"5fde347607439414493441f6fc0fa418","bgimgJsdelivr":"","metaImg":"","author":"Mike Wilson","articleImgCdnMap":{"http://feeds.feedburner.com/~r/BloodyDisgusting/~4/jCj4iTSlFbE":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx31/cdn49@2020_4/2020/09/05/08-45-59-258_60d80c5a4e42db37.webp"},"publishedOrCreatedDate":1599295525722},{"createdTime":"2020-09-05 16:45:25","updatedTime":"2020-09-05 16:45:25","title":"LEGO and Universal Monsters Join Forces for Black & White Frankenstein BrickHeadz Toy!","link":"https://bloody-disgusting.com/?p=3630524","description":"<p>For the first time ever, <strong>LEGO</strong> is headed into the world of the <strong>Universal Monsters</strong> with a <strong>Frankenstein</strong> BrickHeadz toy this Halloween season, previewed by <a href=\"https://www.brothers-brick.com/2020/09/01/lego-reveals-new-universal-monsters-license-with-brickheadz-40422-frankenstein-review/\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener noreferrer\">The Brothers Brick</a>.</p>\n<p>The 108-piece set depicts Frankenstein&#8217;s monster in all his black &#38; white glory, and it could be an indication that many more Universal Monsters LEGO products are on the way.</p>\n<p>The buildable toy, we assume, will be released this Halloween season.</p>\n<p><a href=\"https://www.brothers-brick.com/2020/09/01/lego-reveals-new-universal-monsters-license-with-brickheadz-40422-frankenstein-review/\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener noreferrer\">Head over to The Brothers Brick to learn more and check out an image gallery.</a></p>\n<blockquote class=\"twitter-tweet\">\n<p dir=\"ltr\" lang=\"en\">LEGO reveals new Universal Monsters license with BrickHeadz 40422 Frankenstein [Review] <a href=\"https://t.co/7cQO9KJN1J\">https://t.co/7cQO9KJN1J</a> <a href=\"https://t.co/g9U9fCUK5o\">pic.twitter.com/g9U9fCUK5o</a></p>\n<p>— LEGO Darth Vader (@LegoDarthVader) <a href=\"https://twitter.com/LegoDarthVader/status/1300774437789331457?ref_src=twsrc%5Etfw\">September 1, 2020</a></p></blockquote>\n<p><script async src=\"https://platform.twitter.com/widgets.js\" charset=\"utf-8\"></script></p>\n<img src=\"http://feeds.feedburner.com/~r/BloodyDisgusting/~4/FW09X17acco\" height=\"1\" width=\"1\" alt=\"\"/>","descriptionType":"html","publishedDate":"Fri, 04 Sep 2020 14:37:04 +0000","feedId":13077,"bgimg":"","linkMd5":"6f43a299df1d2cf87013d38c75a785f8","bgimgJsdelivr":"","metaImg":"","author":"John Squires","articleImgCdnMap":{"http://feeds.feedburner.com/~r/BloodyDisgusting/~4/FW09X17acco":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx22/cdn9@2020_6/2020/09/05/08-45-57-909_a57a3dc08b1ddb4c.webp"},"publishedOrCreatedDate":1599295525718},{"createdTime":"2020-09-05 16:45:25","updatedTime":"2020-09-05 16:45:25","title":"Knife-Hand Chucky from ‘Child’s Play 2’ Joins Mezco’s Line of Talking Mega Scale Figures","link":"https://bloody-disgusting.com/?p=3630249","description":"<p>One of the best final acts in a horror franchise sequel can be found in <strong><em>Child&#8217;s Play 2</em></strong>, with Andy and Chucky battling it out in the Good Guys factory. Before being melted into a pile of Garbage Pail Kids-looking goo, Chucky first has his hand ripped clean off. Of course, being the crafty little monster that he is, he quickly finds a new hand in the form of a knife.</p>\n<p>Chucky&#8217;s knife-hand look from <em>Child&#8217;s Play 2</em> has been captured with a couple different toys in recent years, and the latest is an MDS Mega Scale talking figure from <strong>Mezco</strong>!</p>\n<p>Chucky is the first MDS Mega Scale figure to have an interchangeable appendage! His right hand can hold his butcher knife accessory or it can be swapped out for his infamous knife hand.</p>\n<p>The ‘Lakeshore Strangler’ features all-new head sculpt depicting a bloody-nosed, menacing expression after realizing his soul is forever trapped in the body of a doll. Depress the button discretely hidden on his back to hear Chucky speak a total of 7 phrases including &#8220;Alright kid, fun’s over” and “Can&#8217;t keep a good guy down”.</p>\n<p>Sporting his signature ‘Good Guys’ overalls and stripped shirt, Chucky features 11 points of articulation, his trademark orange hair, and realistic glass-like eyes.</p>\n<p>The MDS Mega Scale Talking Menacing Chucky stands 15” tall and comes packaged in a collector-friendly, film-inspired window box.</p>\n<p><a href=\"https://www.mezcotoyz.com/mds-mega-scale-childs-play-2-talking-menacing-chucky?mc_cid=71e47cbfbc&#38;mc_eid=bf95f967ea\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener noreferrer\">You can pre-order the figure for $98, and it&#8217;s set to arrive in March-May 2021.</a></p>\n<p><a href=\"https://i0.wp.com/bloody-disgusting.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/09/chucky-3.jpg?ssl=1\"><img as:</p>\n<ul>\n<li>What is the science behind time travel and parallel universes like in <i>The Dark Tower </i>series and <i>11/22/63</i>?</li>\n<li>How does lack of sleep affect the human body like in <i>Insomnia</i>?</li>\n<li>Is it possible for horrific creatures to exist like in <i>Nightshift</i>?</li>\n<li>What is the science behind curses and legends like +0000","feedId":13077,"bgimg":"https://i0.wp.com/bloody-disgusting.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/09/Poster_Shortcut_GravitasVentures.jpg?resize=740%2C1109&ssl=1","linkMd5":"949bae9fd4d5cd606330fff559230c1d","bgimgJsdelivr":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx29/cdn68@2020_2/2020/09/05/08-45-25-853_c09786237627c432.webp","destWidth":740,"destHeight":1109,"sourceBytes":33952,"destBytes":33952,"author":"Brad Miska","articleImgCdnMap":{"https://i0.wp.com/bloody-disgusting.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/09/Poster_Shortcut_GravitasVentures.jpg?resize=740%2C1109&ssl=1":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx29/cdn68@2020_2/2020/09/05/08-45-25-853_c09786237627c432.webp","http://feeds.feedburner.com/~r/BloodyDisgusting/~4/HHJe1xZLRWw":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx30/cdn46@2020_5/2020/09/05/08-45-57-814_8e77e9011cb1a7a8.webp"},"publishedOrCreatedDate":1599295525722},{"createdTime":"2020-09-05 Horror!","link":"https://bloody-disgusting.com/?p=3630246","description":"<p>The <a href=\"https://bloody-disgusting.com/podcastnetwork/\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener noreferrer\">Bloody Disgusting Podcast Network</a> continues to grow, and the newest member of the family is <strong>The Bloody Disgusting Podcast</strong>!</p>\n<p><em>The Bloody Disgusting Podcast</em> is a weekly horror movie discussion podcast that breaks down the current trending news in the genre, gives a rundown of recent new releases on streaming and VOD, and even offers a listener line where fans can weigh in on the weekly topics. All in a short 60-minute or less episode format, meaning you can get horror’s highlights delivered right to your ears without much time commitment. Think of it as your easily digestible weekly roundup of all things horror.</p>\n<p>The new podcast is co-hosted by Bloody Disgusting’s lead critic and contributor, <a href=\"https://bloody-disgusting.com/author/meagan-navarro/\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener noreferrer\"><strong>Meagan Navarro</strong></a>, <em>Real Queen of Horror</em> blogger and YouTuber <strong><a href=\"https://twitter.com/LovelyZena\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener noreferrer\">Zena Dixon</a></strong>, and the creator of the horror narration podcast <em>Creepy</em>, <strong><a href=\"https://twitter.com/creepypod\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener noreferrer\">Jon Grilz</a></strong>. Listen to these horror fiends discuss horror weekly, with new episodes dropping <strong><em>every Wednesday</em></strong> on your favorite podcast platform.</p>\n<p><strong>The first episode is available now! </strong></p>\n<p>Meagan, Zena, and Jon share what they’ve been watching, break down the news of Netflix’s upcoming series <em>The Haunting of Bly Manor</em>, the new <em>Haunted Mansion</em> movie in the works, and more. Zena curates what’s releasing this week in VOD and streaming. Jon opens up the dedicated listener line so you can send us your thoughts! Favorite responses will get aired the following week.</p>\n<p><strong>Find The Bloody Disgusting Podcast on your </strong><a href=\"https://linktr.ee/BDisgustingPod\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener noreferrer\"><strong>favorite podcast platform</strong></a><strong>, <a href=\"https://www.instagram.com/bdisgustingpod/\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener noreferrer\">Instagram</a>, and </strong><a href=\"https://twitter.com/bdisgustingpod\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener noreferrer\"><strong>Twitter</strong></a><strong>.</strong></p>\n<p><iframe title=\"Spotify Embed: Episode 1\" width=\"100%\" height=\"232\" allowtransparency=\"true\" frameborder=\"0\" allow=\"encrypted-media\" src=\"https://open.spotify.com/embed-podcast/episode/1Qv7qYsOPIjTgrVzlPUD0F?si=93wsT84eTsODE_jbGecfWg\"></iframe></p>\n<p><strong>Make sure to subscribe!</strong></p>\n<img src=\"http://feeds.feedburner.com/~r/BloodyDisgusting/~4/Ln-yWiySaHA\" height=\"1\" width=\"1\" alt=\"\"/>","descriptionType":"html","publishedDate":"Thu, 03 Sep 2020 15:00:50 +0000","feedId":13077,"bgimg":"","linkMd5":"dd2d34274ede0e71ce9a3c8ab3fed81e","bgimgJsdelivr":"","metaImg":"","author":"Meagan Navarro","articleImgCdnMap":{"http://feeds.feedburner.com/~r/BloodyDisgusting/~4/Ln-yWiySaHA":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx25/cdn25@2020_5/2020/09/05/08-45-58-976_b05932cf8903cc31.webp"},"publishedOrCreatedDate":1599295525721},{"createdTime":"2020-09-05 16:45:25","updatedTime":"2020-09-05 16:45:25","title":"‘The Plague of the Zombies’ Delivered a Frightening, Gothic Spin on the Zombie Mythos [Hammer Factory]","link":"https://bloody-disgusting.com/?p=3630407","description":"<p><i>While Hammer Studios has been in business since 1934, it was between 1955 and 1979 that it towered as one of the premier sources of edgy, gothic horror. On top of ushering the famous monsters of Universal’s horror heyday back into the public eye, resurrecting the likes of Frankenstein, Dracula and the Mummy in vivid color, the studio invited performers like Christopher Lee, Peter Cushing, Ingrid Pitt and so many more to step into the genre limelight. Spanning a library housing over 300 films, Hammer Studios is a key part of horror history that until recently has been far too difficult to track down.</i></p>\n<p><i>In late 2018, Shout Factory’s Scream Factory line began to focus on bringing Hammer’s titles to disc in the US, finally making many of the studio’s underseen gems available in packages that offered great visuals as well as insightful accompanying features. Over the course of this column, I will focus on these releases, gauging the films in context of the Hammer Studio story as well as analyzing the merits of the release. It’s time to highlight the power, impact and influence of Hammer Studios and ignite new conversation surrounding some forgotten classics.</i></p>\n<p>Welcome to the <a href=\"https://bloody-disgusting.com/tag/hammer-factory/\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener noreferrer\"><strong>Hammer Factory</strong></a>. This month we dissect <strong><em>The Plague of the Zombies</em></strong>.</p>\n<hr />\n<p><b>The Context</b></p>\n<p>In the back half of 1965, Hammer Studios struck up a partnership with 20th Century Fox that would lead to financing for several of their key properties and secondary films. The pitch was to quickly and efficiently produce a series of double features with an assembly line approach, utilizing much of the same sets, props and crew, generating less expensive films without having to sacrifice the built in marketability of Hammer’s output.</p>\n<p>The first four properties in this deal were produced back to back and then split up into headlining A-style films and accompanying B-level titles. <i>Dracula: Prince of Darkness</i> (1966) and <i>Rasputin the Mad Monk</i> (1966) both starred Christopher Lee and were made as the primary features while <i>The Plague of the Zombies</i> (1966) and <i>The Reptile</i> (1966) were filmed together as the secondary pictures for their respective pairings. All were made at breakneck speed, often with less than one week in between production schedules, leading to months of grueling work for the cast and crew.</p>\n<p>While most of the advertising was allocated to the A-titles, the B-features offered an exciting sense of originality and discovery that something like <i>Dracula: Prince of Darkness </i>sacrificed in lieu of the familiar. Of particular note was <i>The Plague of the Zombies,</i> which dealt in creatures that had been deemed too gruesome to join Universal Studios’ roster of classic monsters several years prior. <strong>Anthony Hinds</strong> and<strong> Peter Bryan</strong>, originally behind the Universal pitch, instead brought the idea to Hammer. As longtime collaborators, the studio was more than willing to give this particular brand of “gruesome” a try, especially given that an American studio was footing the bill.</p>\n<p>The set was a somewhat contentious one, Hammer bringing on trusted director <strong>John Gilling</strong> who was known for his brashness, savage temper and adeptness with marrying the storytelling with the technical side of filmmaking. Somewhat notorious with the cast and crew, he was considered someone who would get the job done, on time and on budget. At the same time, respected actor <strong>André Morell</strong> was brought in to play the lead and wore his immediate and unforgiving distaste for his co-star <strong>Diane Clare</strong> on his sleeve throughout the whole of the production. There’s even some thought that when production wrapped, Morell himself was a factor in why all of Diane Clare’s dialogue was dubbed by <strong>Olive Gregg</strong> without the actress’ knowledge or consent.</p>\n<p>Ultimately the film delivered a frightening, gothic spin on the zombie mythos. With a class based sense of social commentary, it foreshadowed much of the stylistic shifts that would soon be occurring in the genre. Employing chilling effects, rich production design and a discordantly eerie score by <strong>James Bernard</strong>, the picture wowed audiences and created a lasting impression.</p>\n<p>A film which operated several years ahead of its time, <i>The Plague of the Zombies’ </i>influence is as present in the genre today as it was in the flesh-eating glut of films which would come in the wake of George A. Romero’s breakout masterpiece <i>Night of the Living Dead</i> (1968) just two years later. But unlike <i>The</i> <i>Plague of the Zombies</i>, <i>Night of the Living Dead</i> would go on to change the genre and, ironically, provide the first concrete hint that Hammer’s relevance in the marketplace just might have an expiration date.</p>\n<hr />\n<p><b>The Film</b></p>\n<p><iframe class='youtube-player' width='740' height='417' src='https://www.youtube.com/embed/IxjH83cVvUg?version=3&#038;rel=1&#038;fs=1&#038;autohide=2&#038;showsearch=0&#038;showinfo=1&#038;iv_load_policy=1&#038;wmode=transparent' allowfullscreen='true' style='border:0;'></iframe></p>\n<p><i>“Do you believe in life after death, Miss Forbes?”</i></p>\n<p>Men pound ritualistically on drums as two robed figures wearing druidic masks approach a candlelit altar. The score hammers discordantly while the men exchange a small totem, carved to look like a coffin, containing a doll crudely crafted out of clay. Concurrently, a woman awakens in her bed, somewhere far away from the dank cave of dark rites, terrified and bleeding from a wrapped wound on her wrist. Back in the cave, one of the men removes a bottle of what appears to be blood and pours it on the doll, ceremoniously observing his efforts with power and pride.</p>\n<p>Right from the start,<i> The Plague of the Zombies </i>offers a more modern approach to engaging its audience, allowing a glimpse at what might normally play as a late event in the second act. As it is, with its bombastic score and arresting imagery, the sequence unseats expectations and establishes a unique and earthy aesthetic that serves as a contrast to the gothic manors and rustic taverns one might be accustomed to in Hammer’s oeuvre.</p>\n<p>That’s not to say that <i>Plague</i> has any shortage of manors or taverns. Far from it. The film absolutely abides by the tropes of its gothic horror lineage, it simply injects the proceedings with a healthy dose of West Indies Voodoo. As a result, the film offers a sense of seriousness and class that intermingles with a level of grotesquery and horror normally reserved for what might be perceived as a more crude production.</p>\n<p>The film follows Sir James Forbes and his daughter Sylvia (Morell and Clare, respectively) as they travel at the behest of Forbes’ former pupil Peter, played by <strong>Brook Williams</strong>, to a small Cornish village under siege by a mystifying plague. As the town’s physician, Peter is under scrutiny from the community and his own conscience, desperate to discover the source of and solution to the town’s fatalistic dilemma.</p>\n<p><a href=\"https://i1.wp.com/bloody-disgusting.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/09/plague-1.png?ssl=1\"><img data-attachment-id=\"3630422\" data-permalink=\"https://bloody-disgusting.com/editorials/3630407/plague-zombies-delivered-frightening-gothic-spin-zombie-mythos-hammer-factory/attachment/plague-1/\" data-orig-file=\"https://i1.wp.com/bloody-disgusting.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/09/plague-1.png?fit=1363%2C699&#38;ssl=1\" data-orig-size=\"1363,699\" data-comments-opened=\"1\" data-image-meta=\"{&#34;aperture&#34;:&#34;0&#34;,&#34;credit&#34;:&#34;&#34;,&#34;camera&#34;:&#34;&#34;,&#34;caption&#34;:&#34;&#34;,&#34;created_timestamp&#34;:&#34;0&#34;,&#34;copyright&#34;:&#34;&#34;,&#34;focal_length&#34;:&#34;0&#34;,&#34;iso&#34;:&#34;0&#34;,&#34;shutter_speed&#34;:&#34;0&#34;,&#34;title&#34;:&#34;&#34;,&#34;orientation&#34;:&#34;0&#34;}\" data-image-title=\"plague 1\" data-image-description=\"\" data-medium-file=\"https://i1.wp.com/bloody-disgusting.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/09/plague-1.png?fit=300%2C154&#38;ssl=1\" data-large-file=\"https://i1.wp.com/bloody-disgusting.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/09/plague-1.png?fit=740%2C379&#38;ssl=1\" class=\"alignnone size-full wp-image-3630422\" src=\"https://i1.wp.com/bloody-disgusting.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/09/plague-1.png?resize=740%2C380&#038;ssl=1\" alt=\"\" width=\"740\" height=\"380\" srcset=\"https://i1.wp.com/bloody-disgusting.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/09/plague-1.png?w=1363&#38;ssl=1 1363w, https://i1.wp.com/bloody-disgusting.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/09/plague-1.png?resize=300%2C154&#38;ssl=1 300w, https://i1.wp.com/bloody-disgusting.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/09/plague-1.png?resize=1024%2C525&#38;ssl=1 1024w, https://i1.wp.com/bloody-disgusting.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/09/plague-1.png?resize=768%2C394&#38;ssl=1 768w\" sizes=\"(max-width: 740px) 100vw, 740px\" data-recalc-dims=\"1\" /></a></p>\n<p>Despite rumors of André Morell’s distaste for his onscreen daughter Diane Clare, the two exhibit a friendly dynamic that makes their interactions a joy to watch and provides authenticity to their relationship. A classically trained actor, Morell brings gravitas and intensity to the title role, carrying the narrative’s ideological transition from science to superstition with subtlety and impact.</p>\n<p>Although her lines were dubbed over, Diane Clare fares well in the role of curious daughter and concerned friend, although she is mostly relegated to the frightened and eventually brainwashed victim. Brook Williams’ Peter, on the other hand, is distracting to say the least. Requiring heavy emotional output and empathy, I am sad to report that Williams generates neither. Instead, he comes across as huffy and stilted, easily the picture’s weakest link.</p>\n<p>The story sets itself up as a multi-tiered whodunnit, pitting Morell’s Forbes’ scientifically driven mind against the inexplicable nature of disappearing bodies and sightings of corpses roaming the moors at night. Opposite Morell is <strong>John Carson</strong> as Squire Clive Hamilton, acting as the spiritual and financial leader of the village. Carson delivers an understated and yet authoritative masterclass in villainy, which is apparent from the very beginning, despite the protagonists’ ignorance. The film makes no qualms about informing the viewer of its villain’s true intent, presenting the in-story mystery as less of a twisty draw and more of a straight-forward narrative device.</p>\n<p>The frame is lush and beautifully photographed, aside from some rather poorly processed day-for-night sequences, and the effects are well realized. The film contains one of Hammer’s more famous moments of terror when a screeching zombie appears in the night, carrying the corpse of a young woman, but it would be reductive to only mention that over the zombie makeup at large. One scene in particular, involving the undead rising from their graves in the darkness, hands and faces emerging from the grainy earth, feels as effective and relevant to modern day zombie features as most anything made post <i>Night of the Living Dead</i>.</p>\n<p><a href=\"https://i1.wp.com/bloody-disgusting.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/09/plague-of-the-zombies-1.png?ssl=1\"><img data-attachment-id=\"3630424\" data-permalink=\"https://bloody-disgusting.com/editorials/3630407/plague-zombies-delivered-frightening-gothic-spin-zombie-mythos-hammer-factory/attachment/plague-of-the-zombies-1/\" data-orig-file=\"https://i1.wp.com/bloody-disgusting.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/09/plague-of-the-zombies-1.png?fit=1178%2C645&#38;ssl=1\" data-orig-size=\"1178,645\" data-comments-opened=\"1\" data-image-meta=\"{&#34;aperture&#34;:&#34;0&#34;,&#34;credit&#34;:&#34;&#34;,&#34;camera&#34;:&#34;&#34;,&#34;caption&#34;:&#34;&#34;,&#34;created_timestamp&#34;:&#34;0&#34;,&#34;copyright&#34;:&#34;&#34;,&#34;focal_length&#34;:&#34;0&#34;,&#34;iso&#34;:&#34;0&#34;,&#34;shutter_speed&#34;:&#34;0&#34;,&#34;title&#34;:&#34;&#34;,&#34;orientation&#34;:&#34;0&#34;}\" data-image-title=\"plague of the zombies 1\" data-image-description=\"\" data-medium-file=\"https://i1.wp.com/bloody-disgusting.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/09/plague-of-the-zombies-1.png?fit=300%2C164&#38;ssl=1\" data-large-file=\"https://i1.wp.com/bloody-disgusting.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/09/plague-of-the-zombies-1.png?fit=740%2C405&#38;ssl=1\" class=\"alignnone size-full wp-image-3630424\" src=\"https://i1.wp.com/bloody-disgusting.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/09/plague-of-the-zombies-1.png?resize=740%2C405&#038;ssl=1\" alt=\"\" width=\"740\" height=\"405\" srcset=\"https://i1.wp.com/bloody-disgusting.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/09/plague-of-the-zombies-1.png?w=1178&#38;ssl=1 1178w, https://i1.wp.com/bloody-disgusting.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/09/plague-of-the-zombies-1.png?resize=300%2C164&#38;ssl=1 300w, https://i1.wp.com/bloody-disgusting.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/09/plague-of-the-zombies-1.png?resize=1024%2C561&#38;ssl=1 1024w, https://i1.wp.com/bloody-disgusting.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/09/plague-of-the-zombies-1.png?resize=768%2C421&#38;ssl=1 768w\" sizes=\"(max-width: 740px) 100vw, 740px\" data-recalc-dims=\"1\" /></a></p>\n<p>There are of course differences between these zombies and the ones George A. Romero would popularize several years later. The deceased exhibit more vampire-like tendencies than their slavish origins suggest in Voodoo mythos. For example, when Sylvia’s friend Alice, in a consistently scene-stealing performance by <strong>Jacqueline Pearce</strong>, rises from the grave, she moves wearing a wide, devilish grin, suggesting a seductive spell that feels undeniably vampiric.</p>\n<p>The film is not without its flaws. The depiction of the natives drumming madly in the caves is insensitive, somewhat thoughtless and painfully dated. The plot doesn’t always quite add up, which is most glaringly apparent in Hamilton’s inexplicable masterplan to kidnap Sylvia and turn her into a zombie. Still, its inventive take on what was considered a relatively boorish monster at the time allowed the filmmakers to tell a frightening story layered with working class commentary, lending meaning where there might otherwise have only been mild entertainment.</p>\n<p>The movie is fun, frightening and undeniably potent, standing as one of Hammer’s best efforts. It feels fresh despite being beholden to recycled sets and genre tropes, offering up its blood and gore with a social message condemning the elite aristocrats Hammer movies so often served up. Its story plays out remarkably similar to the original <i>Dracula</i> tale, both in plot and character, bringing with it a level of class and contemporary awareness that elevated it far beyond its second-tier classification.</p>\n<p>It’s a rumination on belief, both logical and otherwise, and the overwhelming conviction those under its influence are subject to. Like the pounding of ritualistic drums as they resound through a hollowed out cave, <i>The Plague of Zombies</i> resonates long beyond its brisk runtime, aiding the genre on its path to resurrecting the dead for many years to come.</p>\n<hr />\n<p><b>The Special Features</b></p>\n<p><i>Previously released by Studiocanal in 2012 on Region B blu-ray in the UK, this version comes equipped with the same studio master. Meticulously restored by Pinewood studios, the transfer is clean and detailed. Colors pop and textures are lifelike and engaging. The ported over DTS-HD Master Mono track honors the power of the film’s striking score while still allowing for clarity in dialogue and sound effects, making for a captivating experience overall.</i></p>\n<p><b>Audio Commentary, by Filmmaker Constantine Nasr, Film Historian Steve Haberman and Writer/Producer Ted Newsome</b></p>\n<p><i>(New)</i></p>\n<p>No strangers to Scream Factory’s Hammer line, Constantine Nasr and Steve Haberman return once again, this time with Ted Newsome in tow, to provide their own thoughtful insight regarding the production, players and impact of <i>The Plague of the Zombies</i>.</p>\n<p>They discuss the thematics of the story and its influences, likening it to the Corman-Poe cycle from earlier in the decade as well as looking at the Val Lewton approach it occasionally adopts. They discuss the controversial tactics but undeniable effectiveness of director John Gilling, while also touching on André Morrell’s dislike of Diane Clare and her subsequent re-voicing, suggesting that it may not have been bad acting so much as it was her modern feel which didn’t quite fit the production.</p>\n<p>The historians talk at length about the egregious day for night shooting, calling out that the issue is more with the lab timing and not so much the filmmaker, while still giving kudos to the sequential makeup effects and overall EC Comics feels of the zombies in the picture. They go on to discuss how William Lustig plucked the film from obscurity years ago, licensing it for DVD in the States and the struggles of making forgotten films available for discovery once more.</p>\n<p>It’s a fun and informative track by people who have nothing but respect and admiration for the film. It deepens the personality of the production and is an enjoyable way to further explore the forgotten genre classic.</p>\n<p><b>Audio Commentary, by Author Troy Howarth</b></p>\n<p><i>(</i><i>New</i>)</p>\n<p>The disc also offers a second new commentary track, this time by author and Hammer aficionado Troy Howarth. He provides an incredibly informative, detailed account of the production, the actors and their histories as well as the timeline of the film’s conception through its realization.</p>\n<p>He covers much of the same information as the previous commentary, going deeper into how similar the story is to Bram Stoker’s <i>Dracula</i>. He views the film with an honest eye, making his displeasure with the day for night shooting abundantly clear and laying into Brook Williams performance. He discusses the fascinating dichotomy between the different types of religion and beliefs on display in the film and praises the filmmaking techniques, analyzing the cinematography with the same level of detail he does the performances and anecdotal history of the production.</p>\n<p>Ultimately, the track is a tad dry and a little too encyclopedic when it comes to the filmography of even the smallest onscreen performers, but for fans of the film it is utterly fascinating and his dissection of how the story parallels <i>Dracula</i> is worth the listen alone.</p>\n<p><b>World of Hammer: “Mummies, Werewolves &#38; The Living Dead” (24:55)</b></p>\n<p>(<i>1990, Hammer Film Productions Ltd</i>)</p>\n<p>An episode of Hammer’s TV series, narrated by Oliver Reed. The show was a clip and compilation block that briefly summarized the plots and events from some of the studio&#8217;s most famous films.</p>\n<p>This particular episode primarily contains clips from <i>The Curse of the Mummy’s Tomb</i> (1964), <i>Captain Clegg</i> (1962), <i>Curse of the Werewolf</i> (1961) and <i>The Plague of the Zombies</i>. While offering nothing new, there is a certain wholesome charm to seeing Alice’s decapitation edited with Oliver Reed voiceover in 4&#215;3 standard definition. It reminds of a time when these films were infinitely less available, showing the somewhat lost value of episodes such as this.</p>\n<p><a href=\"https://i2.wp.com/bloody-disgusting.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/09/plague-5.png?ssl=1\"><img data-attachment-id=\"3630425\" data-permalink=\"https://bloody-disgusting.com/editorials/3630407/plague-zombies-delivered-frightening-gothic-spin-zombie-mythos-hammer-factory/attachment/plague-5/\" data-orig-file=\"https://i2.wp.com/bloody-disgusting.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/09/plague-5.png?fit=1358%2C689&#38;ssl=1\" data-orig-size=\"1358,689\" data-comments-opened=\"1\" data-image-meta=\"{&#34;aperture&#34;:&#34;0&#34;,&#34;credit&#34;:&#34;&#34;,&#34;camera&#34;:&#34;&#34;,&#34;caption&#34;:&#34;&#34;,&#34;created_timestamp&#34;:&#34;0&#34;,&#34;copyright&#34;:&#34;&#34;,&#34;focal_length&#34;:&#34;0&#34;,&#34;iso&#34;:&#34;0&#34;,&#34;shutter_speed&#34;:&#34;0&#34;,&#34;title&#34;:&#34;&#34;,&#34;orientation&#34;:&#34;0&#34;}\" data-image-title=\"plague 5\" data-image-description=\"\" data-medium-file=\"https://i2.wp.com/bloody-disgusting.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/09/plague-5.png?fit=300%2C152&#38;ssl=1\" srcset=\"https://i2.wp.com/bloody-disgusting.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/09/plague-5.png?w=1358&#38;ssl=1 1358w, https://i2.wp.com/bloody-disgusting.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/09/plague-5.png?resize=300%2C152&#38;ssl=1 300w, https://i2.wp.com/bloody-disgusting.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/09/plague-5.png?resize=1024%2C520&#38;ssl=1 1024w, https://i2.wp.com/bloody-disgusting.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/09/plague-5.png?resize=768%2C390&#38;ssl=1 768w\" sizes=\"(max-width: 740px) 100vw, 740px\" data-recalc-dims=\"1\" /></a></p>\n<p><b>Raising the Dead: The Making of the Plague of Zombies (35:27)</b></p>\n<p>(<i>2012, Directed by Marcus Hearn, Produced by Studiocanal</i>)</p>\n<p>A series of interviews featuring actor John Carson, actress Jacqueline Pearce, actor Mark Gatiss and film historians Marcus Hearn, Jonathan Rigby and more discussing the making of <i>The Plague of the Zombies</i>.</p>\n<p>Covering everything from John Carson’s frustration that Hammer is what he’s remembered for to the film’s journey from Universal films pitch in 1963 to 20th Century Fox co-produced <i>Dracula: Prince of Darkness</i> B-picture in 1966. The historians offer thoughtful analysis, praising the film’s originality and use of Voodoo zombies in quaint Cornwall while the actors provide charming reminiscence. Jacqueline Pierce in particular livens things up, describing her excitement at seeing herself on the big screen for the first time with <i>Plague </i>and her claustrophobic struggles when making the plaster head for her decapitation scene.</p>\n<p>One of the more fascinating elements of this feature is the time it spends on the film’s restoration. The negative had been badly damaged over time and here they show the excruciating energy and effort Pinewood Studios took to reconstruct the torn and scratched negative, frame by frame.</p>\n<p>While it runs a little long considering it’s mostly comprised of talking heads, it’s an illuminating look at the film. It provides a bite-sized explanation and study of the picture for those who might be interested while not being interested enough to commit to one or both of the commentaries.</p>\n<p><b>Restoration Comparison (3:37)</b></p>\n<p>(<i>2012, Produced by Studiocanal</i>)</p>\n<p>A before and after comparison reel showcasing the amount of depth, color and detail regained by the efforts at Pinewood Studios. Shots of the exterior of the house, the characters conversing and the burning visage of the abandoned tin mine highlight pops, scratches, flickering and skin tone affectations all brought to life in the process of restoring the film. Even giant tears in the frame are corrected here in this incredibly compelling testament to an essential operation oft overlooked by physical media fans.</p>\n<p><b>Theatrical Trailers (7:25)</b></p>\n<p>Three trailers are presented here. The first and second are incredibly similar, the words DRUMS and VOODOO flying at the screen atop the emboldened word TERROR. In classic Hammer fashion, they are laden with hyperbole and far too much plot description, announcing: <i>no corpse can remain at peace in this village of the undead… this land of the zombies!</i></p>\n<p>The third and final trailer focuses on the <i>Dracula: Prince of Darkness</i> double feature. After a minute on Christopher Lee’s returning count, it announces: PLUS — UN DEATH. The second half plays out like the first two trailers, only this time going farther and revealing the final shots of the movie whilst announcing the big reveal of the villain’s master plan.</p>\n<p>The real highlight is seeing the oddly sexist targeted advertisement for boys and girls to get their free Dracula Fangs and Zombie Eyes respectively, as though the two things are gender specific. Not only is it fun to see the emphasis placed on such a gimmick, it shows that Hammer was well aware of the age groups their salacious cinema tended to attract.</p>\n<p><b>Still Gallery (7:10)</b></p>\n<p>Production photography, lobby cards, headshots, glamour shots, candid moments of the cast, crew and effects work and more! Also fun to see are the various posters and advertisements for the stand alone feature and accompanying double bill, spanning the world over. An entertaining slideshow for fans of the film and Hammer alike.</p>\n<hr />\n<p><b>Final Thoughts</b></p>\n<p><a href=\"https://i1.wp.com/bloody-disgusting.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/09/plagye-zombies.png?ssl=1\"><img data-attachment-id=\"3630427\" data-permalink=\"https://bloody-disgusting.com/editorials/3630407/plague-zombies-delivered-frightening-gothic-spin-zombie-mythos-hammer-factory/attachment/plagye-zombies/\" data-orig-file=\"https://i1.wp.com/bloody-disgusting.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/09/plagye-zombies.png?fit=1200%2C720&#38;ssl=1\" data-orig-size=\"1200,720\" data-comments-opened=\"1\" data-image-meta=\"{&#34;aperture&#34;:&#34;0&#34;,&#34;credit&#34;:&#34;&#34;,&#34;camera&#34;:&#34;&#34;,&#34;caption&#34;:&#34;&#34;,&#34;created_timestamp&#34;:&#34;0&#34;,&#34;copyright&#34;:&#34;&#34;,&#34;focal_length&#34;:&#34;0&#34;,&#34;iso&#34;:&#34;0&#34;,&#34;shutter_speed&#34;:&#34;0&#34;,&#34;title&#34;:&#34;&#34;,&#34;orientation&#34;:&#34;0&#34;}\" data-image-title=\"plagye zombies\" data-image-description=\"\" data-medium-file=\"https://i1.wp.com/bloody-disgusting.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/09/plagye-zombies.png?fit=300%2C180&#38;ssl=1\" data-large-file=\"https://i1.wp.com/bloody-disgusting.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/09/plagye-zombies.png?fit=740%2C444&#38;ssl=1\" class=\"alignnone size-full wp-image-3630427\" src=\"https://i1.wp.com/bloody-disgusting.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/09/plagye-zombies.png?resize=740%2C444&#038;ssl=1\" alt=\"\" width=\"740\" height=\"444\" srcset=\"https://i1.wp.com/bloody-disgusting.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/09/plagye-zombies.png?w=1200&#38;ssl=1 1200w, https://i1.wp.com/bloody-disgusting.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/09/plagye-zombies.png?resize=300%2C180&#38;ssl=1 300w, https://i1.wp.com/bloody-disgusting.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/09/plagye-zombies.png?resize=1024%2C614&#38;ssl=1 1024w, https://i1.wp.com/bloody-disgusting.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/09/plagye-zombies.png?resize=768%2C461&#38;ssl=1 768w, https://i1.wp.com/bloody-disgusting.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/09/plagye-zombies.png?resize=1000%2C600&#38;ssl=1 1000w, https://i1.wp.com/bloody-disgusting.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/09/plagye-zombies.png?resize=590%2C354&#38;ssl=1 590w, https://i1.wp.com/bloody-disgusting.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/09/plagye-zombies.png?resize=400%2C240&#38;ssl=1 400w\" sizes=\"(max-width: 740px) 100vw, 740px\" data-recalc-dims=\"1\" /></a></p>\n<p><i>The Plague of the Zombies </i>was a bit of an afterthought, a secondary draw to a far more important headliner. It had neither the stars most associated with Hammer nor the types of recognizable monsters or terrors the studio had spent years basing their image on. It was an oddity, a risk mitigated by the fact that the funding was on 20th Century Fox’s dime and, frankly, it didn’t need to perform— <i>Dracula</i> did.</p>\n<p>Beginning as a failed pitch for a larger studio, the project hung in limbo for years before finally coming to fruition. By the time it reached John Gilling, it had undergone multiple rewrites and budget shifts, landing as a project that Hammer believed in while not being so invested that they cared to micromanage the production. Add in the casting of acclaimed British actor André Morell and the project began to take impressive shape.</p>\n<p>The result was a uniquely original film, despite its typical conceit of an unlikely aged man of prominence investigating some supernatural goings on in a small, secluded town. The effects are fantastic and the zombies themselves truly horrific, alluding to the evolution of the silver screen monster often more associated with the films of the 70s and 80s. It leans on canted angle graveyard shots and lumbering, dead-eyed ghouls just as much as any<i> Of the Dead</i> knock-off well before those films existed to pilfer from in the first place, deserving all the credit and respect that statement should afford.</p>\n<p>Once again, Scream Factory<i> </i>presents a worthy release of an all too under-seen gem. Porting over the great transfer and features found on the 2012 Studiocanal release and commissioning two additional commentary tracks, the release offers the most comprehensive look at the film yet put to disc.</p>\n<p>Who knows if George A. Romero saw this ahead of creating his living dead masterwork. Regardless, I think it’s safe to say that even if Hammer couldn’t keep up with the changing landscape of horror cinema in the coming decade, the studio’s legacy lives in films like <i>The</i> <i>Plague of the Zombies. </i>It’s a history that<i> </i>remains intact and influential, resurrected in its successors and alive in the genre, suggesting that relevance sometimes runs much deeper than ticket sales.</p>\n<p><a href=\"https://i0.wp.com/bloody-disgusting.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/09/plague.jpg?ssl=1\"><img data-attachment-id=\"3630415\" The odds of a robber breaking into your home is a lot higher than, say, encountering a rampaging werewolf. Because the genre has long since capitalized on this fear, fans have grown somewhat desensitized to home invasion thrillers. While the invasion of one’s home remains a prevalent anxiety in modern society, it’s still hard to get excited about a well-worn concept if it doesn’t offer any new angle or subversion. While </span><strong><em>The Owners</em></strong><span data-preserver-spaces=\"true\"> doesn’t attempt to break the mold, it instead opts for a peculiar brand of insanity to complement the violence.</span></p>\n<p><span data-preserver-spaces=\"true\">Based on the graphic novel </span><em><span data-preserver-spaces=\"true\">Une Nuit de Pleine lune</span></em><span data-preserver-spaces=\"true\"> by Hermann and Yves H., </span><em><span data-preserver-spaces=\"true\">The Owners</span></em><span data-preserver-spaces=\"true\"> opens with a trio of unsavory characters sitting in a trash-filled car, scoping out a large estate in a countryside. As soon as the owners leave, they break in, ransack the place but come up empty. Mary (<strong>Maisie Williams</strong>), a girlfriend hoping to get her car back to head into work, is an unintentional accomplice. Her boyfriend and his friends opt to wait inside for the owners to come home. They find out that they picked the wrong people to mess with. Naturally, it escalates into a night of violence no one saw coming.</span></p>\n<p><img data-attachment-id=\"3628297\" data-permalink=\"https://bloody-disgusting.com/the-owners_9/\" data-orig-file=\"https://i1.wp.com/bloody-disgusting.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/08/THE-OWNERS_9.jpg?fit=1200%2C800&#38;ssl=1\" data-orig-size=\"1200,800\" data-comments-opened=\"1\" https://i1.wp.com/bloody-disgusting.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/08/THE-OWNERS_9.jpg?resize=300%2C200&#38;ssl=1 300w, https://i1.wp.com/bloody-disgusting.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/08/THE-OWNERS_9.jpg?resize=768%2C512&#38;ssl=1 768w, https://i1.wp.com/bloody-disgusting.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/08/THE-OWNERS_9.jpg?w=1200&#38;ssl=1 1200w\" sizes=\"(max-width: 740px) 100vw, 740px\" data-recalc-dims=\"1\" /></p>\n<p><span data-preserver-spaces=\"true\">The comparisons to </span><em><span data-preserver-spaces=\"true\">Don’t Breathe</span></em><span data-preserver-spaces=\"true\"> will be inevitable; a plot of unlikable characters breaking into the home of unassuming, elderly homeowners seems eerily similar, after all. Beyond that, </span><em><span data-preserver-spaces=\"true\">The Owners</span></em><span data-preserver-spaces=\"true\"> takes a very different approach. The film never bothers any attempt to provide rooting interest for any of its characters. Mary’s boyfriend, Nathan (<strong>Ian Kenny</strong>), barely shows the smallest glimpses of humanity among a string of terrible, mean-spirited decisions. His pal Terry (<strong>Andrew Ellis</strong>) shows reticence at causing harm, but it’s overshadowed by his man-baby persona and creepy obsession with Mary. The worst among them is thug Gaz (<strong>Jake Curran</strong>), a nasty human through and through. Mary’s by far the most likable of the group, but even she is prone to making reprehensible choices. This is the type of thriller that decides to wedge in unnecessary character devices like a pregnancy to engender audience sympathy. In other words, there’s no redemption in any of our leads, making it difficult to invest in what happens to them.</span></p>\n<p><span data-preserver-spaces=\"true\">Luckily, director/writer <strong>Julius Berg</strong> and his co-writer <strong>Mathieu Gompel</strong> offer some reprieve in the form of brutal violence and a pair of eccentric homeowners. <strong>Sylvester McCoy</strong>’s Dr. Huggins is a scene-chewing foil who&#8217;s making the most of a dour story. Wife Ellen Huggins (<strong>Rita Tushingham</strong>) might be even loonier than her counterpart, injecting welcome manic energy and unpredictability to how this night plays out. There&#8217;s torture and death aplenty, and it’s delightfully gory. If anything upstages McCoy’s bonkers portrayal of an equally bonkers character, it’s <strong>Scarlett O’Connell</strong>’s (</span><em><span data-preserver-spaces=\"true\">The Girl with All the Gifts</span></em><span data-preserver-spaces=\"true\">) makeup design. It’s so good you wish there were more heinous characters injected into the mix, simply so you could watch them die in gruesome ways, too.</span></p>\n<p><span data-preserver-spaces=\"true\">Berg does an excellent job highlighting the kills and moments of excruciating mayhem, but beyond that, </span><em><span data-preserver-spaces=\"true\">The Owners</span></em><span data-preserver-spaces=\"true\"> is a fairly standard thriller without any frills. That is, save for a third act aspect ratio change that ultimately adds nothing to the conversation. Then again, <em>The Owners</em> doesn’t have much to say in the first place.</span></p>\n<p><em><span data-preserver-spaces=\"true\">The Owners</span></em><span data-preserver-spaces=\"true\"> offers a solid enough entry in home invasion thrillers, one in which there are no heroes. Other than its bizarre brand of weird, there’s not much else that’s unique about this entry of the subgenre. That means it might entertain for a while if you can look past grating protagonists, but it won’t stay with you after the credits roll.  </span></p>\n<p><strong><em>The Owners</em> releases in theaters and VOD on September 4, 2020.</strong></p>\n<p><a href=\"https://i2.wp.com/bloody-disgusting.com/wp-content/uploads/2012/11/2-5skullrating.png?ssl=1\"><img data-attachment-id=\"3201907\" data-permalink=\"https://bloody-disgusting.com/news/3201902/album-review-flyleaf-new-horizons/attachment/2-5skullrating/\" data-orig-file=\"https://i2.wp.com/bloody-disgusting.com/wp-content/uploads/2012/11/2-5skullrating.png?fit=224%2C64&#38;ssl=1\" data-orig-size=\"224,64\" data-comments-opened=\"1\" data-image-meta=\"{&#34;aperture&#34;:&#34;0&#34;,&#34;credit&#34;:&#34;&#34;,&#34;camera&#34;:&#34;&#34;,&#34;caption&#34;:&#34;&#34;,&#34;created_timestamp&#34;:&#34;0&#34;,&#34;copyright&#34;:&#34;&#34;,&#34;focal_length&#34;:&#34;0&#34;,&#34;iso&#34;:&#34;0&#34;,&#34;shutter_speed&#34;:&#34;0&#34;,&#34;title&#34;:&#34;&#34;}\" data-image-title=\"2-5skullrating\" data-image-description=\"\" data-medium-file=\"https://i2.wp.com/bloody-disgusting.com/wp-content/uploads/2012/11/2-5skullrating.png?fit=224%2C64&#38;ssl=1\" data-large-file=\"https://i2.wp.com/bloody-disgusting.com/wp-content/uploads/2012/11/2-5skullrating.png?fit=224%2C64&#38;ssl=1\" class=\"alignnone size-full wp-image-3201907\"
